(August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> although it remains relatively high in the former. However, in the industrialized Asian nations such as <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, teenage birth rates remain among the lowest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-escap_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-escap-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The overall trend in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> since 1970 has been a decreasing <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a>, an increase in the age at which women experience their first birth, and a decrease in the number of births among teenagers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Most continental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_European" title="Western European">Western European</a> countries have very low teenage birth rates. This is varyingly attributed to good <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex education</a> and high levels of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraceptive" title="Contraceptive">contraceptive</a> use (in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_values" title="Traditional values">traditional values</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">social stigmatization</a> (in the case of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>) or both (in the case of <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy_and_sexual_health_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Teenage pregnancy and sexual health in the United Kingdom">Teenage pregnancy and sexual health in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>The teen pregnancy rate in England and Wales was 23.3 per 1,000 women aged 15 to 17. There were 5,740 pregnancies in girls aged under 18 in the three months to June 2014, data from the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a> shows. This compares with 6,279 in the same period in 2013 and 7,083 for the June quarter the year before that. Historically, the UK has had one of the highest teenage pregnancy and abortion rates in Western Europe.</p>
<p>There are no comparable rates for conceptions across Europe, but the under-18 birth rate suggests England is closing the gap. The under-18 birth rate in 2012 in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a> was 9.2, compared with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU" title="EU">EU</a> average of 6.9. However, the UK birth rate has fallen by almost a third (32.3%) since 2004 compared with a fall of 15.6% in the EU. In 2004, the UK rate was 13.6 births per 1,000 women aged 15–17 compared with an EU average rate of 7.7.</p>
<p>A spokeswoman for the <a href="/wiki/British_Pregnancy_Advisory_Service" title="British Pregnancy Advisory Service">British Pregnancy Advisory Service</a> said: "Contrary to popular perception, this data shows that the teenage pregnancy rate is falling dramatically in England and Wales. While the UK has historically had a high teenage conception rate, it is now at its lowest level on record and not significantly out of step with other European countries.</p>
<p>"We have seen a huge decline in the number of babies born to teenage mothers over the last decade, in part due to the improvements we've seen in contraception advice and services for younger women, with straightforward access to abortion services when their chosen method lets them down. But it also reflects broader societal shifts, with younger women quite rightly expecting and able to pursue educational and professional ambitions."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy_in_the_United_States" title="Teenage pregnancy in the United States">Teenage pregnancy in the United States</a></div>
<p>The teenage birth rate in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> is the highest in the developed world, and the teenage abortion rate is also high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-45">[45]</a></sup> In 2005 in the U.S., the majority (57%) of teen pregnancies resulted in a live birth, 27% ended in an induced abortion, and 16% in a fetal loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The U.S. teenage pregnancy rate was at a high in the 1950s and has decreased since then, although there has been an increase in births out of wedlock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The teenage pregnancy rate decreased significantly in the 1990s; this decline manifested across all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" title="Race (classification of human beings)">racial groups</a>, although teenagers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kinship_and_descent" title="Kinship and descent">descent</a> retain a higher rate, in comparison to that of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European-American" title="European-American">European-Americans</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian-American" title="Asian-American">Asian-Americans</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Guttmacher_Institute" title="Guttmacher Institute">Guttmacher Institute</a> attributed about 25% of the decline to <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abstinence" title="Sexual abstinence">abstinence</a> and 75% to the effective use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraception" title="Contraception">contraceptives</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> While in 2006 the U.S. teen birth rate rose for the first time in fourteen years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> it reached a historic low in 2010: 34.3 births per 1,000 women aged 15–19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Historic-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The latest data from the United States shows that the states with the highest teenage birthrate are <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a> while the states with the lowest teenage birthrate are <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadian</a> teenage birth has also trended towards a steady decline for both younger (15–17) and older (18–19) teens in the period between 1992 and 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teenpregna_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-teenpregna-111">[111]</a></sup> However, teen pregnancy has been on the rise since 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teenage_fatherhood">Teenage fatherhood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Teenage fatherhood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In some cases, the father of the child is the husband of the teenage girl. The conception may occur within wedlock, or the pregnancy itself may precipitate the marriage (the so-called <a href="/wiki/Shotgun_wedding" title="Shotgun wedding">shotgun wedding</a>). In countries such as <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> the majority of teenage births occur within marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-escap_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-escap-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In other countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, the majority of teenage mothers are not married to the fathers of their children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd_45-7"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In the UK, half of all teenagers with children are lone parents, 40% are cohabitating as a couple and 10% are married.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Teenage parents are frequently in a romantic relationship at the time of birth, but many adolescent fathers do not stay with the mother and this often disrupts their relationship with the child. U.S. surveys tend to under-report the prevalence of teen fatherhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In many cases, "teenage father" may be a misnomer. Studies by the Population Reference Bureau and the National Center for Health Statistics found that about two-thirds of births to teenage girls in the United States are fathered by adult men aged over 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The Guttmacher Institute reports that over 40% of mothers aged 15–17 had sexual partners three to five years older and almost one in five had partners six or more years older.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> A 1990 study of births to California teens reported that the younger the mother, the greater the age gap with her male partner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In the UK 72% of jointly registered births to women aged under 20, the father is over 20, with almost 1 in 4 being over 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Teenage pregnancy was normal in previous centuries, and common in developed countries in the 20th century. Among Norwegian women born in the early 1950s, nearly a quarter became teenage mothers by the early 1970s. However, the rates have steadily declined throughout the developed world since that 20th century peak. Among those born in Norway in the late 1970s, less than 10% became teenage mothers, and rates have fallen since then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-20th_century">Pre-20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Pre-20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>It is often said that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" title="Virgin Mary">Mary</a>, the mother of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>, was aged 12 to 14 when she became pregnant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hildegard_of_Vinzgouw" title="Hildegard of Vinzgouw">Hildegard of Vinzgouw</a>, the second wife of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, was about 14 years old when she gave birth to her first son in 772 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1187 <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Hainault" title="Isabella of Hainault">Isabella of Hainault</a> was aged 17 when she gave birth to <a href="/wiki/Louis_VIII_of_France" title="Louis VIII of France">Louis VIII of France</a>, but she died in 1190 aged 19 the day after giving birth to twin boys; both boys died 3 days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Isabel_de_Clare,_4th_Countess_of_Pembroke" title="Isabel de Clare, 4th Countess of Pembroke">Isabel de Clare</a> and all five of her daughters were teenage mothers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Violant_of_Aragon" title="Violant of Aragon">Violant of Aragon</a> queen consort of <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a> gave birth to her first three children before she was 20 in 1256.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1230 Isabel Bigod, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Bigod,_3rd_Earl_of_Norfolk" title="Hugh Bigod, 3rd Earl of Norfolk">Hugh Bigod, 3rd Earl of Norfolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maud_Marshal" title="Maud Marshal">Maud Marshal</a>, became a widow aged 18 with 3 children. She went on to have at least six more children with her second husband <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_FitzGeoffrey" title="John FitzGeoffrey">John FitzGeoffrey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_Beaufort,_Countess_of_Richmond_and_Derby" title="Margaret Beaufort, Countess of Richmond and Derby">Margaret Beaufort</a>, the mother of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>, was 13 years old when she gave birth to him in 1457. The birth was particularly difficult due to her physical immaturity and small size and she would never give birth again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> She feared for her eldest granddaughter, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Tudor" title="Margaret Tudor">Margaret Tudor</a>, and would not allow her to be sent to her husband <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_IV" title="James IV">James IV</a> in Scotland until she was grown enough. Even so, the younger Margaret gave birth to her first three children before she was 20 in 1509; all three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Died_in_infancy" title="Died in infancy">died in infancy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Singer <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Darin" title="Bobby Darin">Bobby Darin</a> was born to a teenage mother in 1936, whom he believed to be his sister for most of his life, until she revealed to him as being his actual mother in his adult life. He was never told the identity of his true father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li>Child actress turned diplomat <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Temple" title="Shirley Temple">Shirley Temple</a> was 19 when she gave birth to her first child, Linda Susan, in 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EdwardsP355_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-EdwardsP355-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WindelerP68_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-WindelerP68-135">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ann_Dunham" title="Ann Dunham">Ann Dunham</a> was 18 when in 1961 she gave birth to her son, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_US_Presidents" title="List of US Presidents">44th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Naomi_Judd" title="Naomi Judd">Naomi Judd</a> gave birth to <a href="/wiki/Wynonna_Judd" title="Wynonna Judd">Wynonna Judd</a> on May 30, 1964, the same day her high school diploma was mailed to her. Wynnona was born Christina Claire Ciminella; Michael Ciminella was not the biological father but married Naomi to give Christina his surname.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah Winfrey</a> was 14 when she gave birth to a boy, who died shortly after birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biography_Channel_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biography_Channel-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dimple_Kapadia" title="Dimple Kapadia">Dimple Kapadia</a> was 17 when she gave birth to <a href="/wiki/Twinkle_Khanna" title="Twinkle Khanna">her first daughter</a> and 19 when she gave birth to <a href="/wiki/Rinke_Khanna" title="Rinke Khanna">her second daughter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tamara_Beckwith" title="Tamara Beckwith">Tamara Beckwith</a> dropped out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheltenham_Ladies%27_College" title="Cheltenham Ladies' College">Cheltenham Ladies' College</a> in order to have her daughter, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Anouska_Poppy_Pearl&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Anouska Poppy Pearl (page does not exist)">Anouska Poppy Pearl</a> in 1987. The father was an American Marine. Anouska is now studying acting in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dwayne_Michael_Carter_Jr." title="Dwayne Michael Carter Jr.">Dwayne Michael Carter Jr.</a> (Lil Wayne) had his baby, Reginae, with his now ex-wife Antonia "Toya" Johnson when he was 15 and she 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Pop singer <a href="/wiki/Fantasia_Barrino" title="Fantasia Barrino">Fantasia Barrino</a>, winner of <a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a> 2004, was 16 when she gave birth to a daughter named Zion Quari' in 2001; in 2005 she released a controversial song about single motherhood titled "Baby Mama."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taylor_Hanson" title="Taylor Hanson">Taylor Hanson</a>, a member of the pop band Hanson, was 19 when his 18-year-old wife Natalie gave birth to their first child, a son named Jordan Ezra, in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yulia_Volkova" title="Yulia Volkova">Yulia Volkova</a>, of the controversial Russian pop band <a href="/wiki/T.A.T.u." title="T.A.T.u.">t.A.T.u.</a>, was 19 when she gave birth to her daughter Viktoria Pavlovna Volkova in September 2004; she had spoken publicly about having an abortion the year before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li>Singer and actress <a href="/wiki/Solange_Knowles" title="Solange Knowles">Solange Knowles</a>, the younger sister of singer <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>, was 18 when she gave birth to her first child, Daniel Julez Smith Junior, in October, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asia_Nitollano" title="Asia Nitollano">Asia Nitollano</a>, who joined the pop group The Pussycat Dolls after winning a reality TV show, was 17 when she gave birth to her daughter in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oscar-nominated actress <a href="/wiki/Keisha_Castle-Hughes" title="Keisha Castle-Hughes">Keisha Castle-Hughes</a> was 17 when she gave birth to her first child, a girl named Felicity-Amore, in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></li>
<li>Actress and singer <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Lynn_Spears" title="Jamie Lynn Spears">Jamie Lynn Spears</a>, younger sister of pop singer <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, gave birth to a daughter in 2008 when she was 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bristol_Palin" title="Bristol Palin">Bristol Palin</a>, 18, the teenage daughter of <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>'s <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008 vice presidential candidate</a> former<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Alaskan Governor <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Palin" title="Sarah Palin">Sarah Palin</a>, gave birth on December 27, 2008 to a son named Tripp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lou_Doillon" title="Lou Doillon">Lou Doillon</a>, French actress and daughter of <a href="/wiki/Jane_Birkin" title="Jane Birkin">Jane Birkin</a>, gave birth to son Marlowe Jack Tiger Mitchell in 2002 at age 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Times-155">[155]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teenage_pregnancy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some politicians condemn pregnancy in unmarried teenagers as a drain on taxpayers, if the mothers and children receive welfare payments from the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
